  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bd27a34f-342e-46f5-9b78-47e0b6bcb7f6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7594299201512212985" style="display:none">Twenty years ago Claire Scott's eldest sister, Julia, went missing. No one knew where she went - no note, no body. It was a mystery that was never solved and it tore her family apart.<br /><br />Now another girl has disappeared, with chilling echoes of the past. And it seems that she might not be the only one.<br /><br />Claire is convinced Julia's disappearance is linked.<br /><br />But when she begins to learn the truth about her sister, she is confronted with a shocking discovery, and nothing will ever be the same...</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/584945-why-aren-t-there-some-warnings-that-is-has">Why aren&#39;t there some warnings that is has dark subject matter, torture, rape and violence to women? I assumed that it would skirt around some issues... You know it&#39;s happening, but it&#39;s not really detailed. But, that&#39;s not the case. There is some really touchy subject matter in this book and it may not appeal to everyone. I think there needs to be a warning to just people know.</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It is funny that you all want to read murder filled crime thrillers without the actual crime. Don't want to be forced to care about the victims or kno<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It is funny that you all want to read murder filled crime thrillers without the actual crime. Don't want to be forced to care about the victims or know their experience. You should place the same warning you propose on your bibles. <br /><br />Of course she knew the PC police would be out with their torches and pitchforks. Kudos to Karin for ignoring your delicate sensibilities and challenging the status quo. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_803').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>    </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1186060559" />
    <a title="Karin Slaughter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10901279-karin-slaughter"><img alt="Karin Slaughter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565730663p2/10901279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1186060559?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin Slaughter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin Slaughter" href="/user/show/10901279-karin-slaughter">Karin Slaughter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)
          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24371990-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1186060559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13864532503480462460">Authors are always asked where they get their ideas, and the truth is that most of the time we don't know. An idea is a weird thing--usually, it's like a grain of sand that your brain worries into a pearl. When did the sand start to turn into something shiny and beautiful? No way to know.<br/><br/>WIth PRETTY GIRLS I actually know when I got the idea. Maybe it was somewhere in the back of my brain all along, but I actually woke up from a dream and had the idea firmly in my head (okay, that doesn't tell yo</span>
  <span id="freeText13864532503480462460" style="display:none">Authors are always asked where they get their ideas, and the truth is that most of the time we don't know. An idea is a weird thing--usually, it's like a grain of sand that your brain worries into a pearl. When did the sand start to turn into something shiny and beautiful? No way to know.<br /><br />WIth PRETTY GIRLS I actually know when I got the idea. Maybe it was somewhere in the back of my brain all along, but I actually woke up from a dream and had the idea firmly in my head (okay, that doesn't tell you where it comes from, but that's as close as I can get. Oh, and can I add that I was taking Tramadol for a slipped disc, so maybe that had something to do with it?)<br /><br />Anyway, I loved the idea so much that I scrapped the book I had planned for this year (2015*) and started working on the storyline for what became PRETTY GIRLS. I was on fire, I tell ya! The characters were so firmly cemented in my mind by the time I sat down to write the first scene that it was almost like I was taking dictation.<br /><br />You'll probably hear a lot about characters and the literary merits (ha ha, I hope!) but make no mistake--at its heart, this book is a thriller. There are lots of twists and turns and all the stuff that folks have come to expect from me. The only thing missing is cops. Not that there aren't cops in the story (because they usually show up when there's a crime) but the narrators are just two ordinary women who are thrown into extraordinary circumstances. The real question is whether or not they can rise to the occasion (or will they make it at all?)<br /><br />I really hope y'all enjoy the book. And don't worry--the next book for 2016 will have Will Trent and Sara Linton. I appreciate your patience because I know y'all love Will and Sara, but long-time readers will know what happens when I get bored and I wanted to take a knee on Will and Sara so that I could take time with the next phase of their stories together. <br /><br />*wahhhh!!!! WHEN DID I GET TO OLD????</span>
  <a data-text-id="13864532503480462460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1400507033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1400507033" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1400507033?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1400507033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14895041673609509377">In 1991 Julia Carroll disappeared. Her body was never found. In the following years the family coped in very different ways. The mother while forever quietly grieving, moved on and made a new life for herself. The father spent years looking for any clue as to what happened. Sisters Claire and Lydia grieved in very different ways and were estranged having not spoken in many years. Now over twenty years later, there has been another disappearance of a teenage girl and a murder of a middle-aged man</span>
  <span id="freeText14895041673609509377" style="display:none">In 1991 Julia Carroll disappeared. Her body was never found. In the following years the family coped in very different ways. The mother while forever quietly grieving, moved on and made a new life for herself. The father spent years looking for any clue as to what happened. Sisters Claire and Lydia grieved in very different ways and were estranged having not spoken in many years. Now over twenty years later, there has been another disappearance of a teenage girl and a murder of a middle-aged man that seem to be connected. This causes the sisters to reunite. <br /><br />I have found that over the last year I've read quite a few stories about missing girls/children etc. Although this book is about WAY more than a missing girl. There is so much going on in this book right from the start. The twists start early on. This book really shows how a crime affects everyone involved. How differently everyone copes, not just when the crime is first committed but how it can shape the actions and futures of all involved. <br /><br />At the very beginning I found it a little difficult to get all the POVS straight. However, I was quickly drawn into the lives of these women and other characters, trying to figure out how the many separate story lines connected.<br /> <br />After I was well into the book I started to realize that the gruesomeness might be too much for me. I was starting to skip over the descriptions (very graphic descriptions) and feeling quite bothered. Other readers may not have an issue with it but I just felt a bit overloaded with details of such horrific acts. I ended up having to skip over quite a few parts.<br /><br />I understand it's a thriller and it was to show just how much of a monster certain characters were but it's rare that I have to skip so much or put down a book because I'm so horrified. In my opinion gruesome violence overkill. At the same time the authors ability to describe other things and situations so well kept me intrigued as to what was going to happen next. At certain parts I was literally holding my breath as things were unfolding. Just like watching a horror movie and yelling "don't go in there" to the person on the screen I wanted to yell similar things at Claire and Lydia. <br /><br />Throughout the book my heart hurt for all of the families. I can't even imagine some of the things described happening. There really are some things that can't be unseen. Heartfelt and heartbreaking you could feel the love Sam had for his family as he bared his soul in letters to his missing daughter. <br /><br />The end was quite moving, so I am glad I finished the book. However, I don't know that I would put myself though that again. It was just a bit much for me. I may consider reading some of Karin Slaughter's other books but I will choose wisely. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14895041673609509377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1399193740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399193740" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399193740?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062429056" href="/book/show/25465056-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399193740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14068055802335146487">I just want to start by saying I don't want to list any spoilers here; I think this book was so powerful that I would hate to discourage someone from reading it because I took away from their experience before even beginning the book.<br/><br/>Wow! This book was heavy. I just can't think of a better word to sum up how I feel after finishing this. I'm glad I spaced it out instead of devouring it like I wanted to initially. I've seen many people torn on this book and I understand why; it is EXTREMELY graphi</span>
  <span id="freeText14068055802335146487" style="display:none">I just want to start by saying I don't want to list any spoilers here; I think this book was so powerful that I would hate to discourage someone from reading it because I took away from their experience before even beginning the book.<br /><br />Wow! This book was heavy. I just can't think of a better word to sum up how I feel after finishing this. I'm glad I spaced it out instead of devouring it like I wanted to initially. I've seen many people torn on this book and I understand why; it is EXTREMELY graphic and disturbing. Content and descriptions. I know some of the subjects are triggers for many people, especially women. For me, I felt the extreme graphic violence was necessary to put the power behind the punch of the storyline. I have felt lately that nothing really "shocks" me in a book anymore, almost like I've read too many graphic stories. This one was different.<br /><br />The plot is connecting the stories of 2 young women who have gone missing decades apart- Julia Carroll and Anna Kilpatrick. Without giving too much away, the journey is told from the viewpoint of Julia's two remaining sisters- Lydia and Claire, while inserting occasional diary entries from their father, Sam Carroll.<br /><br />I loved the layout of how the story was told; the diary entries interwoven between chapters of the current storyline. I had to go back once to reread because it was so clever. I think we can all agree whether we like her brutal style or not that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> is an excellent storyteller and master of her craft. I'm an avid fan but am willing to admit that in her previous standalone, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18594594.Cop_Town" title="Cop Town by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Cop Town</a> while a great story, had a bit of excess descriptive fluff IMO. I was pleased to see this one didn't seem to have that; I felt every word was needed. I found myself literally holding my breath and sitting upright at times.<br /><br />I felt she did a good job relaying the anguish of a family who has lost a child. A loss this deep affects everyone and it literally tore them apart. I did feel it a little hard to connect with Lydia/Claire at times and I really would have liked to have seen a little more development with Rick and Dee. One of my favorite chunks of the book was near the end with Helen and Claire as we are reaching the climax of the action; I felt this was the most well written part of the entire book. <br /><br />Overall, I wavered between giving this one 4-5 stars and ended up rounding up. I felt this book was extremely well written, the story kept my attention constantly-this is the definition of a suspenseful thriller. While the graphic violence was extremely disturbing, I felt it did not distract me from the story (personally) but can understand why it would have for anyone. Overall, if you are a Slaughter fan, I would HIGHLY recommend. If you are new to her as an author, I would recommend starting with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a> in the Grant County series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14068055802335146487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24371990-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223643999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17555623864013121892">My reaction to learning a new book was out by one of my favorite authors.<br/><br/>A new Karin Slaughter!!!!!!!!<br/><br/>My reaction after reading this book.<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/CXqsiei' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790543.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I love this author. I fangirl so hard over her Grant County/Will Trent books so much that if I go anywhere that has them I must be restrained from recommending that people read them. Yes, Library ladies I will try and behave.<br/>But this one. Not.<br/>It didn't even feel like it was written by the same author that I love.<br/><br/>It starts off with Claire Scott. She is a ty</span>
  <span id="freeText17555623864013121892" style="display:none">My reaction to learning a new book was out by one of my favorite authors.<br><br>A new Karin Slaughter!!!!!!!!<br><br>My reaction after reading this book.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/CXqsiei" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790543.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I love this author. I fangirl so hard over her Grant County/Will Trent books so much that if I go anywhere that has them I must be restrained from recommending that people read them. Yes, Library ladies I will try and behave.<br>But this one. Not.<br>It didn't even feel like it was written by the same author that I love.<br><br>It starts off with Claire Scott. She is a typical Buckhead Barbie <br><a href="http://imgur.com/Moj0UzF" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439061026i/15790544.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Perfect husband, lots of money, no job. Just looking pretty all day.<br>Then she meets her husband Paul for dinner one night. As they are leaving old boring Paul wants to put some moves on her in a dark alley. Claire is a bit freaked out that Paul is up to this because he usually doesn't get frisky unless it's in the actual bedroom, so she wants some spark and follows him to the alley. A bad guy attacks and Paul is murdered. (This is not a spoiler because it happens very early and won't ruin any of the book)<br><br>Once she returns home Claire gets to looking on Paul's computer for some files that his business partner wants and she finds way more than she bargained for. <br>Now this is happening in the middle of so much other stuff that your mind is racing at this point of the book. You have Claire's sister Lydia telling some of the story from her viewpoint, a break in at Claire's house, and a sister that had gone missing years ago. Then throw in another recent missing girl from the area.<br><br>So much going on. <br>Then the tropes started...<br><a href="http://imgur.com/8K5jAph" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790545.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://imgur.com/wRBmTdo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://imgur.com/gFIJ2Zr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790547.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://imgur.com/26i3Q5X" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then throw in about a thousand times on how very beautiful our main character is...she is pretty and smart. *insert gag here*<br><a href="http://imgur.com/CDV9bfH" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061026ra/15790549.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://imgur.com/QNU6jwu" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061027ra/15790550.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://imgur.com/tL2ccXQ" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439061027ra/15790551.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That got old real quick. Karin Slaughter is usually better than this. So I gave one of my favorite authors a two star review. Does that mean I will not grab up her next one? Of course not. I will fangirl the next time. Hopefully.<br><br><i>Book source: Edelweiss in exchange for review.</i><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17555623864013121892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1342964618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1342964618" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1342964618?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342964618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10083452309272165560"><blockquote>
  <b> The world stops for you when you’re pretty. That’s why women spend billions on crap for their faces. Their whole life, they’re the center of attention. People want to be around them just because they’re attractive. Their jokes are funnier. Their lives are better.</b>
</blockquote>Well, there might be <i>some</i> downsides. <i>Pretty Girls</i> is a white-knuckle thriller that will keep you turning the pages long after you should really have gone to sleep. Do not read this while on a train. You will miss your stop.<br/><br/>The story</span>
  <span id="freeText10083452309272165560" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> The world stops for you when you’re pretty. That’s why women spend billions on crap for their faces. Their whole life, they’re the center of attention. People want to be around them just because they’re attractive. Their jokes are funnier. Their lives are better.</b>
</blockquote>Well, there might be <i>some</i> downsides. <i>Pretty Girls</i> is a white-knuckle thriller that will keep you turning the pages long after you should really have gone to sleep. Do not read this while on a train. You will miss your stop.<br><br>The story is told from three alternating perspectives. Claire Scott, newly free of that nasty ankle-monitor, has a pretty good life. 38, in great shape, no kids, a studly, attentive hubby who makes much more than a decent living, cool digs. What’s not to like? After a celebratory dinner out, Paul wants to do the nasty in an adjacent alley, way out of character, but, whatever. But sorry, no nookie for you guys. An armed, tattooed criminal element sort robs them. Things go too far and Paul winds up on the sidewalk, tinting the pavement with considerable quantities of red, and the game is afoot. What Claire discovers in going through her late mate’s computer files after the funeral will rock her world. <br><br>Lydia Delgado’s life is somewhat different. Single mother, 41, struggling to get by, alienated from most of her family, runs a dog grooming business. Her past would not look very nice on a resume. She’d hit rock bottom a while back and lived there for a spell, with a pick and shovel. But these days she is respectable. Owns a dog-grooming business. Met her pretty nice bf in a 12-step program. Her teenage daughter is a peach. Lydia is on the wrong side of pudge these days, with an addiction to the sort of culinary drugs that come in crinkly bags at supermarkets. Life’s a bitch and then you diet. Lydia used to be a looker. Not surprising, really. Her sisters were easy on the eyes too, but one vanished when she was 19, never to be seen again, and the other one just saw her husband get killed. <br><br>Sam is a determined sort, bulldog with a bone. He never believed the official cop line that his Julia had simply run away. So he dedicated his life to finding out what had <i>really</i> happened to his eldest daughter. It cost him his marriage, and maybe even more. We see the progress of Sam’s investigation through his journals, from the time when he was on this quest. Claire and Lydia’s adventure takes place today.<br><br>The two sisters join forces to continue searching for the truth about Julia’s disappearance, and must face the consequences of Claire learning some very disturbing secrets about her husband.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438324850i/15693370.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Karin Slaughter</b> - from her FB pages<br><br>Karin Slaughter is not new to the best-seller lists, having sold more than 30 million copies of her crime books in 32 languages. She was born in a small Georgia town and now lives in Atlanta, where <i>Pretty Girls</i> is set. Her books include six in the Grant County series and nine in the Will Trent series, set in Atlanta. She was working on another book entirely when the notion for this one occurred to her in a dream, so she checked in with her publisher, put the planned book on the back burner and dove into this one. <br><br>There are several elements at work here. In a book of this sort, if you are not engaged by the characters, the rest does not much matter. Lydia certainly has had her troubles in the past, but she is pretty supportable now, finding her best self in this worst of times. Claire makes us wonder how she could have buried her head in the sand for so long, ignoring what look like warning signs to us. But in wondering, it is worth keeping in mind that we are all sand-dwellers, from the neck up at least. Maybe it is an innate and useful skill to be able to simply ignore warning signs of peril. If we recognize them then we might have to do something about them, which entails personal risk, of either physical or emotional harm. Most of the time most of us prefer to keep a lid on things. Thus we live to ignore another day. So it feels entirely credible that reasonable people can overlook behavior that might stand out to an external observer. Particularly in Claire’s case, as she has tried to keep her head down in most situations for most of her life. We can see her vulnerability, however cloaked it may have been, and can easily feel for her. In addition we see the characters develop over the course of the tale, Claire moving from passive to assertive and Lydia moving from nobody to a sort of anti-hero. Family dynamics plays a major part in the sisters’ struggle, both to find the truth and to find a way back to sisterhood across a very large distance. Check.<br><br>The story must be engaging. Will Claire and Lydia find out what really happened to their missing sister? Does Sam? Do we care? If you can’t empathize with this as a driving force, it must be because you are too busy torturing kittens. Check.<br><br>Pace must be maintained. Slaughter must have a metronome that is set for increasing tempo. Check. <br><br>The baddie must be truly scary, and up to some really awful stuff. You have no idea. Check<br><br>The hero/heroine(s) must face believable peril. Is it possible that one or more of our core three might come to harm of the terminal sort? You betcha. Check<br><br>A thriller is never without a bit of misdirection, a few fish-hooks hoisting red-herrings for us to consider. Yep. Get your scaling tools ready. Check.<br><br>And there is that old favorite, the twist. Let’s just say that <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8fUNSBvNur4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Chubby Checker</a> would be pleased. Check. Wait, what’s that? My advisors inform me that not everyone will appreciate my lame boomer refs, so, fine, whatever. For you kids out there, ok, rewind. Start over. Twists. Let’s just say that after reading this book, I was in need of a good neck brace. Ok? Sheesh.<br> <br>Finally there is the issue of payload. That is the extra information one learns about the world in reading a work of fiction. I suppose there is a bit of that here. I have no idea if the awfulness that is depicted in <i>Pretty Girls</i> (aside from Paul’s questionable taste in décor and labeling) has a real-world basis. Although it does seem that if one can imagine a particularly grotesque form of depravity, there is probably someone, somewhere who is practicing it right now, and with so many folks on the planet, probably more than a few. So if the book is highlighting some actual form of human awfulness, then bad-a-bing. Check <br><br>Gripes. You knew there would have to be one or two. The title, <i>Pretty Girls</i> suggests that those on the 10 side of life are more at risk than those closer to the 1 end of things. The theme of prettiness is noted with frequency early on, in comments on the attractiveness of some and the unattractiveness of others. Slaughter seems interested in giving some serious thought to how people react to beauty and to how the beautiful react to the world. Certainly there is peril about for those blessed with pleasing countenances, whether it comes from a <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PW_02k7LRMo" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">wicked witch</a> or the <a href="https://vimeo.com/74033442" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ravages of time</a>. She keeps up the mentions for a while, sometimes offering actual insight. But then it seems to fade, as if she had run out of things to say about prettiness, until it is brought back into the spotlight for a final bow or two. Like, oh, the title is <i>Pretty Girls</i>. I guess I should put something in here to give that some closure. It looked totally like an afterthought. I thought this could have been better handled, maybe spread out a bit more, maybe dig a bit more than skin deep. But that is a quibble. No one is going to read this book to get enlightened about beauty. My second gripe will have to be a bit clouded. I don’t want to spoil anything. I found the particular fixation of the baddie on the specific group that is targeted curious. Why did this person focus on these targets? I did not get that there was a particular reason why the baddie was so set on this particular subset of victims. Perhaps the significance of this is in the eye of the beholder? But no matter, really. <br><br>The bottom line here is that you will be ripping through this book, dying (well, almost) to see how things turn out. <i>Pretty Girls</i> is an outstanding thriller, a very engaging, entertaining, and disturbing read, and that is a beautiful thing. <br><br>Review posted – 7/31/15<br><br>Publication date – 9/29/15<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://www.karinslaughter.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> pages<br><br>How serial killers <a href="https://serialkillersvictimschoosing.wikispaces.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">choose</a> their victims<br><br>The Advantages of Being Beautiful<br>---<a href="http://www.businessinsider.com/studies-show-the-advantages-of-being-beautiful-2013-6" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">8 Scientifically Proven Reasons Life Is Better If You're Beautiful </a> – by Dina Spector in Business Insider<br>---A Smithsonian article on <a href="http://www.smithsonianmag.com/science-nature/how-much-is-being-attractive-worth-80414787/?no-ist" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <br>How Much is Being Attractive Worth</a> - by Abigail Tucker<br>---<a href="http://www.spring.org.uk/2011/08/10-pleasures-and-pains-of-being-beautiful.php" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">10 Pleasures and Pains of Being Beautiful</a> by Dr Jeremy Dean on <i>PsyBlog</i><br><br>A lovely <a href="http://www.literaryweek.com/interviews/KarinSlaughterInterview.mp3" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">audio interview</a> with the author by Steve White of <i>Literary Week</i>. The sound levels are off a bit, his volume being too loud relative to hers, but it’s worth putting up with.<br><br>July 23, 2020 - Slaughter offers up some commentary on her book in GR’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/notes/40017404-pretty-girls/10901279-karin-slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Kindle Notes &amp; Highlights</a> - some nice intel there - check it out<br><br><br>====================================<b>SONGS</b><br><br>Offering a bit of further discomfort, after reading this book you might find some of these listens a bit disturbing<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_PLq0_7k1jk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Pretty Woman </a> – Roy Orbison and friends<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pBQ-S6njQQw" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Oh You Pretty Things </a> - David Bowie<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VYXqwbtkkeM=" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">PYT (Pretty Young Thing)</a> - Michael Jackson<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6m_xsrHquow" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">You’re Beautiful</a> – James Blunt<br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z6xfpLqn5IM" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">You are so Beautiful</a>– Joe Cocker<br><br>And the all time best stalker theme song - <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OMOGaugKpzs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Breath You Take</a> - The Police</span>
  <a data-text-id="10083452309272165560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2353464474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2353464474" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2353464474?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2353464474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14314185540872250135">4.5 stars. This book truly blew me away. I was not a huge fan of the story in the beginning but once it picked up, I could not put it down.<br/><br/>CW: murder, violence, gore, torture, rape, assault<br/><br/>This novel is straight up disturbing and horrifying. I don’t believe I have ever read a more graphic and chilling novel. As someone who spends a decent amount of time listening to readings of “dark web stories” and other horror stories on YouTube and scrolling through reddit threads like /letsnotmeet and /nosl</span>
  <span id="freeText14314185540872250135" style="display:none">4.5 stars. This book truly blew me away. I was not a huge fan of the story in the beginning but once it picked up, I could not put it down.<br /><br />CW: murder, violence, gore, torture, rape, assault<br /><br />This novel is straight up disturbing and horrifying. I don’t believe I have ever read a more graphic and chilling novel. As someone who spends a decent amount of time listening to readings of “dark web stories” and other horror stories on YouTube and scrolling through reddit threads like /letsnotmeet and /nosleep, this book fed into my fascination with wickedness in humanity. This book is truly not for the faint of heart. It is sick and twisted and surely will leave a lasting impression on all readers.<br /><br />After reading <i>The Good Daughter</i> as well, I can say with confidence that Karin Slaughter is extremely talented at writing complex family dynamics. I loved learning about Claire and Lydia’s history, uncovering the reason behind their falling out, and watching them piece their relationship together in the direst of situations. <br /><br />The beginning of the novel did not totally grasp me. The plot was a big slow to start as we are introduced to the characters and it took me a bit of time to really become engaged with the story. For me, there was not one particular moment that hooked me so I was surprised to find that at some point during reading, I just could not put the story down. This novel quickly transforms from mundane to thrilling and chilling and I’m so pleased I continue through the end.<br /><br /><i>Pretty Girls</i> was a truly fantastic read. I would definitely recommend it to my fellow lovers of thrillers, but more specifically to those who can stomach heavy, grotesque content.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14314185540872250135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

While I think Slaughter relies heavily on shock value and violence to be intriguing, I still appreciate the emphasis on family and the bond between the two sisters (even though it is limited to just white feminism, as there's some casual racism that's kind of a turn-off).</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14287753879243969367">This book was so damn freaking spectacular that I don't even know where to start. This has climbed to the top of my list as my favorite psychological thriller ever. This tops Dark Places and That Night and I never thought that would happen! For any book to triumph over those is a win for me :) although they are still right behind this book.<br/><br/>I've never read a book like this.   <span id="freeText14287753879243969367" style="display:none">This book was so damn freaking spectacular that I don't even know where to start. This has climbed to the top of my list as my favorite psychological thriller ever. This tops Dark Places and That Night and I never thought that would happen! For any book to triumph over those is a win for me :) although they are still right behind this book.<br /><br />I've never read a book like this. There are so many twists and turns a race car driver would have trouble navigating. I literally cannot stop thinking about all of the people and events in this book. I went into it with just the knowledge that this was about a woman and her sister that hadn't spoken for years and that was about it. Holy moly did this get good!<br /><br />I simply cannot say enough good things about Pretty Girls. The plot is terrifying yet makes you want to read on because you have to know what happens. Literally every chapter gives you a new twist. The characters are so real I could picture them inside of my mind as I read and the scenery... I could see it all.<br /><br />Karin Slaughter knows how to write a terrifying mystery. If I could give this 100 stars I would.<br /><br />It needs to be made into a movie for sure. It would have record breaking ticket sales!<br /><br />Go read this. NOW!</span>

<div id="review_1523447924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523447924" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523447924?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/26544752-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=organized-crime">organized-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dark-themes">dark-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=wtf-did-i-just-read">wtf-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=rich-guys">rich-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523447924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12465419661139558226">Check out more of my reviews at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookaddicthaven.com'>www.bookaddicthaven.com</a><br/><br/>Wow! This was one dark and disturbing story. I love dark reads, but this was pretty gruesome for me at times. I was at the edge of my seat from start to finish with this one. I even had nightmares about this book. As I start to write this review, just thinking about it is giving me the chills. It was just that messed up.<br/><br/>When Claire Scott is widowed by her wealthy, seemingly perfect husband, she is left to pick up the pieces. With the FBI and</span>
  <span id="freeText12465419661139558226" style="display:none">Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a><br /><br />Wow! This was one dark and disturbing story. I love dark reads, but this was pretty gruesome for me at times. I was at the edge of my seat from start to finish with this one. I even had nightmares about this book. As I start to write this review, just thinking about it is giving me the chills. It was just that messed up.<br /><br />When Claire Scott is widowed by her wealthy, seemingly perfect husband, she is left to pick up the pieces. With the FBI and the local police showing a suspiciously high interest in her husband's murder, and the subsequent break-in at their home, Claire does not know what to think. When she stumbles upon some computer files of her husband's, she begins to question the very foundation of her marriage and what she really knew about the man she married.<br /><br />From beginning to end, this book was full of twist and turns. Everyone was a suspect at some point and you never knew who you could trust. As Claire partnered up with her estranged sister, Lydia, to try and sort through the clues her husband inadvertently left behind, the truth seems to become less and less clear. <br /><br />Claire's husband, Paul, was not who he said he was. He had secrets...big secrets. The more the sisters unearth, the greater the danger. They can't turn back, but they don't know where to turn for help either.<br /><br />At the center of this book is a string of missing teenaged/college-aged girls, including Claire and Lydia's own sister, Julia. Unsolved disappearances with undeniable commonalities, which all somehow connect back to Paul. Everything is not as it seems though. Claire begins to suspect that there is involvement at the highest levels, protecting those responsible for these horrible crimes.<br /><br />If you like psychological suspense/thrillers, then this is a great story. Be forewarned, this book is very graphic and downright gory. It contains detailed descriptions of barbaric torture, sexual assault and murder. The sick and twisted actions of this serial killer are not left to the imagination. If you cannot handle the graphic descriptions of torture, then this is not a book for you. I'm a big fan of dark stories and it gave me a nightmare or two.<br /><br />Overall, I thought that it was a fantastic story. It was suspenseful and kept me in a hyper-vigilant state until every question had been answered. I had chills while listening to this story. This has got to be one of the most screwed up, disturbing stories that I've "read". <br /><br />I listened to the Audible version of this book and it was great. The narration was well-done. I found it to be an excellent audiobook selection that was easy to follow. The mood and emotions were conveyed clearly, which is sometimes hard to come by in an audiobook. I could almost touch the fear and the anxiety in "Claire's" voice. Kudos to the narrator(s).<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12465419661139558226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1411200315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411200315" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411200315?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411200315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13188094109294680043"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED :::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444355731i/16488752.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>HOLY HELL. </b>So, I just spent the last 2 days reading this awesome book. It went waaaaaay the freaking hell outside of my "usual" reading preferences. The genre is more of a <u>
  <strong>crime thriller</strong>
</u> (no romance) which I almost never read but this particular blurb really grabbed me. So I opened the book. By the end of the prologue, I had CHILLS running through me and tears in my eyes.... So, I had to read it!!! And honestly I loved it!!<br/><br/>But you guys, it is <u>NOT</u> for the fain</span>
  <span id="freeText13188094109294680043" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED :::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444355731i/16488752.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>HOLY HELL. </b>So, I just spent the last 2 days reading this awesome book. It went waaaaaay the freaking hell outside of my "usual" reading preferences. The genre is more of a <u>
  <strong>crime thriller</strong>
</u> (no romance) which I almost never read but this particular blurb really grabbed me. So I opened the book. By the end of the prologue, I had CHILLS running through me and tears in my eyes.... So, I had to read it!!! And honestly I loved it!!<br><br>But you guys, it is <u>NOT</u> for the faint of heart. The story starts out small but the "mystery" just gets deeper and deeper and deeper. And every new thing you discover is this whole other level of creepy.<br><br>Please note that there is <u>graphic violence</u> in this book (not a lot in terms of content, but what there is will make <em>anyone</em> shudder and cringe. However, if you're used to watching TV shows like Criminal Minds or CSI, you'll probably be ok to read this (it's kind of on the same level that they have). But it's still very seriously  G.R.A.P.H.I.C.  and genuinely disturbing at times. Please be warned.<br><br>This is also a book with absolutely <u>no fluff</u>. You can't skim <em>anything</em> because you'll miss crucial elements or reveals. It's intricate and layered. This author clearly spent a great deal of time <em>plotting out </em>her story before writing it because everything happens for a reason, every piece of the story has a purpose, and by the end, they all fit together. One reason I'm always wary of thrillers is I rarely find them <em>satisfying </em>but this book gave <u>every single answer</u> to every single question. I'm a fast reader and will usually breeze through full-length book in an afternoon but it took me 2 days to read this (3 technically since I read the first 10% one night, and the rest over 2 days) because there was just so MUCH going on in it...<br><br>*deep breath*<br><br>First, I'm going to share the blurb with you (because it was the blurb that made me want to read it):<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Sisters. Strangers. Survivors.<br><br>More than twenty years ago, Claire and Lydia’s teenaged sister Julia vanished without a trace. The two women have not spoken since, and now their lives could not be more different. Claire is the glamorous trophy wife of an Atlanta millionaire. Lydia, a single mother, dates an ex-con and struggles to make ends meet. But neither has recovered from the horror and heartbreak of their shared loss—a devastating wound that's cruelly ripped open when Claire's husband is killed.<br> <br>The disappearance of a teenage girl and the murder of a middle-aged man, almost a quarter-century apart: what could connect them? Forming a wary truce, the surviving sisters look to the past to find the truth, unearthing the secrets that destroyed their family all those years ago . . . and uncovering the possibility of redemption, and revenge, where they least expect it.<br> <br>Powerful, poignant, and utterly gripping, packed with indelible characters and unforgettable twists, Pretty Girls is a masterful novel from one of the finest writers working today.</i>
</blockquote><br>And next, I'm going to actually show you guys all my status updates now (NO SPOILERS) so you can sort of see what I went through while reading it... (haha, sorry, I can get a bit sweary sometimes)<br> <br>	 2% -- What an <em>amazing</em> prologue!!! I have chills, shivers, tears. Totally hooked! <br>	 3% -- <em>So</em> INTO this story!!!! <br>	 5% -- Ok I'm seriously freaking out. Can I handle this?? I'm a romance reader, dammit. I need my swoon (even my <em>dark</em> reads have swoon!!!) and this is freaking me the fuck out!!!!! *keeps reading* <br>	 6% -- FUCK. dammit. holy crap. Am I strong enough to read this?! Let's find out *eyes book warily* <br>	 7% -- SMART SMART SMART BRILLIANT FUCKING WRITING!!! <br>	 8% -- okayyyyyy, did NOT see that reaction coming. That must be one helluva history they’ve got there for <em>THAT</em> to be her reaction. O.O <br>	 10% -- chills and shivers again. How amazing is this writing?? I hate that I have to go to bed now because <em>I want to keep reading!!</em> <br>	 11% — back to reading today. I've seriously been more surprised, shocked, impressed, intrigued, in the first 10% of this book than I have been by most complete books! <br>	 16% — Woah. Wait, she did WHAT now?? <br>	 16% — Holy freaking fuckkkkkkk *GAAAASP* Well that just about calls EVERYTHING into question. <br>	 19% — I love the attention to detail. Like how the sister of a girl who’d been abducted would then take natural precautions in her life — like teach her child how to change a tire so she’d never be stuck on the side of the road, or always scan the parking lot before unlocking the car doors. Smart! <br>	 24% — my brain is overloaded with theories right now. SO MANY possibilities! <br>	 26% — red pill/blue pill &lt;-- love that reference <br>	 29%— such an interesting line.<br><em>“He isolated her.”</em><br><em>“Sounds like a classic abuser.”</em><br><em>“As far as I know, he never hit her or even raised his voice at her. He just </em>kept<em> her.”</em> <br>	 32% — Ahhhhh, love this!!! <em>“He had been so very, very cunning, hiding all of his transgressions in plain sight. The only question now was how many more transgressions was she going to find?”</em> <br>	 34% — holyyyyyyy shit. no WAY!! <br>	 36% — yeah, I’m with Lydia on this sentiment:<em> “What the fuck, Claire?” She stared at Claire with open shock. "What the fucking fuck?”</em> <br>	 37% — hehe that was badass. <em>“I’ve never told anyone this... but it felt so fucking good to be bad.”</em> <br>	 39% — ****spoiler removed**** I really wish I could share that line with you. SO GOOD! <br>	 44% — this just gets more and more complex …. like <em><strong>woah!</strong></em> <br>	 47% — Ok, I actually have a secondary theory which explains 95% of everything. But that other 5% is still weirding me the fuck out!!!  (note: I was wrong about this theory, guess that darn 5% mattered) <br>	 53% — <em>“I can’t just walk away from this. I have to know. There isn’t anything left in my life except finding out the truth.” &lt;--- </em>my sentiments exactly! *keeps reading* <br>	 55% — <strong>holy. freaking. HELL. ****** GASP *******<br></strong>Okay. WARNING: this book is graphically violent. It's very similar in to Criminal Minds or CSI in terms of the level if you want a comparison point. <br>	 57% — NO. WAYYYYYYYYY. <em>How????</em> <br>	 67% — definitely not for the faint of heart. Fair warning, I literally just cringed away from the page.... and also OMG!!!!!!!!! O_O <br>	 68% — this story goes to show that you really don’t need a paranormal story to show true evil. Sometimes, humans can make the very worst monsters of all. <br>	 69% — Okay I’ve been reading this for the last 3 hours straight and I have to go to bed. This is definitely a book you have to FOCUS on. There’s no skimming or light reading or you’ll miss important facts. Its 421 pages and there is NO FLUFF. <br>	 70% — back to it (next day). This book is like one <em>holy shit</em> moment after another. And each pause between them only serves to build to the next jaw dropping reveal. <br>	 73% — <em>“You haven’t talked to each other in twenty years and now you’re suddenly worried about her daughter?" -- </em><em>“Lydia is my sister. Even when I hated her, I still loved her.”</em> <br>	 75% — ok seriously. This is pretty gruesome. If you’re sensitive to graphic violence, this book is <u><em>not for you</em></u>. Please be warned. <br>	 79% — holy exposition batman. I feel like I've just have this flood of information streaming into my head for the last few percents. It almost feels like this book will never end. I don't mean that in a bad way but there's just <em>so much</em> going on. <br>	 85% — Omg. I love her mom!!!!!!! That was pretty badass! <br>	 88% — Graphic, gruesome, disturbing, gory violence. Like seriously. stomach-turning. <br>	 97% — Just WOAH. That was an <em>INTENSE</em> last few percents. I feel like I've been holding my breath and just flipping pages like mad. And that scene though..... Karma is a bitch! <br>	 100% — Wow that last line. <em><strong>Wow!</strong></em> How strangely beautiful for such a chilling story as this. Definitely a beautiful way to end things. Loved the book! <br> <br>Ok so without giving anything away, I'll just tell you guys that there <u>is</u> a very satisfying ending. Note again that this is <em>not a romance</em> (at all) but everything is wrapped up in the ending and actually the last line was absolutely <em>perfect</em>. Seriously, just really STRONG writing!<br><br>Nothing about this book is 'expected'. Even the nature of the crime itself is one that I honestly hadn't ever seen before (at least not this extreme) on any crime-fighting TV show. *shudders* The story keeps you on your toes, catching you off guard with it's surprises over and over again. There's never a dull moment.<br><br>The story is told in third person from three main perspectives. Claire and Lydia's (the two estranged sisters of the abducted girl from the 90's) perspectives that begin separately but entwine later on, and their father's -- though his was through forms of journal entries written addressed to his missing daughter. I found it fascinating the way it showed how much perspective mattered. One person could see someone as a monster, and to another person, they could be a savior. It was chilling.<br><br>Karin Slaughter truly has some of the strongest writing I've read. Like seriously. It doesn't matter if you end up loving or hating the story, it doesn't change the fact that the <em>writing</em> itself is top notch. The reason I rare read other genres is that they're rarely able to hold my attention -- I <em>crave</em> the emotional connection in romances -- so it's a real testament to how good this writing was that I was that <em>into</em> this story.<br><br>So, at this point I'm still a little in shock from this story, but I absolutely don't regret reading it and even though it was <em>totally</em> completely utterly <u>different</u> than my usual beloved romance reads, I loved this too (even though I'm honestly a little creeped out still, lol). It was a really fantastic "change of pace" read for me. Y'know? Sometimes you just need one of those. I like stepping outside my comfort zones every now and again to try something different. I find it kind of refreshes me for when I step back into my romance reads. Haha, buuuuuuuut I'm gonna need something light, sexy, and fun next!!!<br><br>Really though. If you're into thrillers, <em>definitely</em> try this book. If you're not into thrillers but still curious, I'd recommend this as a great one to try because it's genuinely <u>good</u>. As I'm writing this, it was released last week and it actually hit #4 on the New York Times Best Sellers list this week. And yes, I <em>know</em> it's really expensive, which is why I never posted any updates while I was reading. I wanted to be <em>sure</em> I'd finished it and could actually stand by suggesting it before I began posting about it. But yes, it's definitely a great book and one I'd easily recommend for someone looking for a really solid read within this genre!<br><br><strong>Rating: ahhh I have no idea how to put these thoughts to a rating. I'm disturbed by the some of the content of the story but I loved the book and <u>loved</u> the writing. Can you guys just accept "really freaking great thriller" to be my rating, please? </strong><br><br><b>STANDALONE. CRIME THRILLER. <br>(this is absolutely not a romance) </b><br><br>_______________________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521374012" />
    <a title="Megan Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31853583-megan-johnson"><img alt="Megan Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523045365p2/31853583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1521374012?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Johnson" href="/user/show/31853583-megan-johnson">Megan Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062429056" href="/book/show/25465056-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31853583-megan-johnson?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31853583-megan-johnson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1521374012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2153418214698756731">What would you do if suddenly everything you thought you knew was ripped away from you and you were left to figure out how to make it all on your own? What if that wasn't all and you were also faced with uncovering the dark and wicked pasts of those you thought you loved?<br/><br/>Karin Slaughter's Pretty Girls asks all of the questions and then answers them in the creepiest way I can imagine. It's been a while since I laid in bed at night hoping that what I had just read doesn't give me nightmares, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText2153418214698756731" style="display:none">What would you do if suddenly everything you thought you knew was ripped away from you and you were left to figure out how to make it all on your own? What if that wasn't all and you were also faced with uncovering the dark and wicked pasts of those you thought you loved?<br /><br />Karin Slaughter's Pretty Girls asks all of the questions and then answers them in the creepiest way I can imagine. It's been a while since I laid in bed at night hoping that what I had just read doesn't give me nightmares, but this one had me doing just that. Add that on top of the fact that I absolutely couldn't put this book down, and we've got a real winner on our hands.<br /><br />Pretty Girls is the story of two sisters, one whom has just found herself widowed and the other a single mother of a teenaged daughter. They've long been estranged but have recently found themselves in communication again. Little do they know that uncovering their past will uncover way more than they ever could have expected - including some new clues regarding the 20 years ago disappearance of their oldest sister.<br /><br />This book is full of twists and unexpected moments right from the beginning. In fact, after reading the first chapter I was able to notice that my heart was racing. After debating whether or not I could pass that off as my cardio workout for the day, I kept going and was sucked into the craziness that continued to transpire page after page. I do feel like I've read a lot of books recently that jump around in terms of POV (point of view), but after I got used to the flow of this one it was like putting together a puzzle in terms of connecting all of the pieces. And just as you might a puzzle, after I completed it I found that everything finally made complete sense...which is so gratifying.<br /><br />Fair warning, this book is very much a thriller and contains graphic moments of sexual content and violence. However, that's part of what makes it so enthralling within it's genre. I might be too much for some to handle but if you're up for it, I can't even begin to recommend this book enough.<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://www.tipsywriter.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a> | <a href="http://www.twitter.com/tipsy_writer" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/tipsywriter" rel="nofollow noopener">FACEBOOK</a> | <a href="http://www.instagram.com/tipsywriter" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2153418214698756731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1474753554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474753554" />
    <a title="Basil Sidebottom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46957477-basil-sidebottom"><img alt="Basil Sidebottom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442202371p2/46957477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1474753554?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Basil Sidebottom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Basil Sidebottom" href="/user/show/46957477-basil-sidebottom">Basil Sidebottom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1474753554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674911010325278698">Here's the thing.<br/><br/>The book is full of torture porn. It's about 400 pages and I'd say 1/4 is straight up, highly detailed repetitive torture porn. That's about 100 pages describing women being tortured, raped and murdered. And cut up.<br/><br/>This isn't your run-of-the-mill thriller. No, no. This is big kid stuff. The stuff that gets called "chilling" and "heart pounding" and "edge of your seat" and "thriller" and "psychological".<br/><br/>No.<br/><br/>What it is, is DULL.<br/><br/>Don't get me wrong. I'd say the first 140 pages or so,</span>
  <span id="freeText7674911010325278698" style="display:none">Here's the thing.<br /><br />The book is full of torture porn. It's about 400 pages and I'd say 1/4 is straight up, highly detailed repetitive torture porn. That's about 100 pages describing women being tortured, raped and murdered. And cut up.<br /><br />This isn't your run-of-the-mill thriller. No, no. This is big kid stuff. The stuff that gets called "chilling" and "heart pounding" and "edge of your seat" and "thriller" and "psychological".<br /><br />No.<br /><br />What it is, is DULL.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. I'd say the first 140 pages or so, it's engaging, almost gripping. <br /><br />And then the first big thing happens and then almost immediately a second. Me? I felt my heart sink. Because anyone who's seen a 90s thriller, Lifetime movie or not, should be able to rattle off the next few major plot points in easy succession.<br /><br />And they'd be right.<br /><br />So the plot? Garbage. It goes from one level of ludicrous to the next. You may even laugh at the last big 'twist' the book reveals. Because it's stupid. Soap operas have more flair. This is a paint by numbers tale. People behave in a manner that might work in a Monty Python sketch. There's an FBI agent that acts and speaks as though he's stumbled in from another goddamn dimension, and all you want to do is punch him in the face. <br /><br />Oddly enough, the purest bits, the best and profound parts are the journal entries that dot the path of this terrible story. They are from a grieving father to the missing daughter he can never give up on. I read each one, grateful, because THOSE kept me going, pushing me to the end. <br /><br />Because it certainly wasn't the torture porn and the third act that ratchets up everything to a lunatic finish.<br /><br />In the end, you might feel as I did. A bit numb. Grossed out that you'd picked it up and spent hours of your life actually consuming the work. Astonished at the number of critics who insisted the level of violence was not gratuitous when it was nothing BUT gratuitous. <br /><br />Library folk? Take off the mystery label you might place on the spine of this book. Put on a horror label instead. People deserve at least SOME sort of warning.<br /><br />First, last and only book by this author I'll look at.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7674911010325278698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3025600397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9002738750045363029"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>This was one of the hardest books to read that I’ve ever read. It has trigger warnings for pretty much any awful thing you can imagine like: violent rape, sexual assault, suicide, graphic violence, murder, torture, and at times I honestly wasn’t sure if I could stomach any more of it. But I was captivated by this writing and I couldn’t stop reading this book, I had to figure out how it would end.<br/><br/><b>This is my first book from Karin Slaughter</b> and it definitely won’t be my last, though it may</span>
  <span id="freeText9002738750045363029" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br />This was one of the hardest books to read that I’ve ever read. It has trigger warnings for pretty much any awful thing you can imagine like: violent rape, sexual assault, suicide, graphic violence, murder, torture, and at times I honestly wasn’t sure if I could stomach any more of it. But I was captivated by this writing and I couldn’t stop reading this book, I had to figure out how it would end.<br /><br /><b>This is my first book from Karin Slaughter</b> and it definitely won’t be my last, though it may be a while before I pick up another because my heart hurts right now. It mainly follows two sisters Claire and Lydia who haven’t spoken in years, but when Claire’s husband is murdered, their horrible past comes back to them. <br /><br />This book was incredibly hard to read, and it made me cringe so many times. I don’t think I’ve ever read torture like this and the way it was described literally made my stomach roll. I would not recommend this book to just anyone, because this shit is super fucked up. But this story really drew me in. It is an edge-of-your-seat thriller from page 100 till the end. And by the ending I was literally bawling my eyes out for this family. <b>I don’t think a thriller has ever made me cry until this one.</b> After finishing this book I feel emotionally drained.</span>
