<div id="review_3383019975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3383019975" />
    <a title="Arini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39722464-arini"><img alt="Arini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565922259p2/39722464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3383019975?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arini" href="/user/show/39722464-arini">Arini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40017404-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Arini by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/62566585-embibliophile">EmBibliophile</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3383019975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5970906074571242977"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>Pretty Girls</i> hammers the point home that men is the worst thing that’s ever happened to humanity. . .<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591721365ra/29619928.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is some seriously effed up story. It’s graphic and appalling and will probably give you nightmares, especially if you’re a girl. Particularly, the pretty ones with blond hair. Cause you know, some bogeymen are just so . . . <i>basic</i> and more vain than the others.<br/><br/><blockquote>
<b>Claire</b> and <b>Lydia</b> had a sister who vanished twenty years ago. When Claire’s husband is suddenly killed, the two estranged sis</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5970906074571242977" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br><i>Pretty Girls</i> hammers the point home that men is the worst thing that’s ever happened to humanity. . .<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591721365ra/29619928.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is some seriously effed up story. It’s graphic and appalling and will probably give you nightmares, especially if you’re a girl. Particularly, the pretty ones with blond hair. Cause you know, some bogeymen are just so . . . <i>basic</i> and more vain than the others.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>Claire</b> and <b>Lydia</b> had a sister who vanished twenty years ago. When Claire’s husband is suddenly killed, the two estranged sisters decided to reunite and work together to find out the connection between the murder and Julia’s disappearance.<br><br><b>TW:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[violence against women, rape, snuff porn, suicide, substance abuse. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</blockquote><br>The most interesting and twisted aspect of this book is the crime itself. The plot drags and relies copiously on shock value and gory violence. It’s quite predictable and tropey but not so boring that you’ll lose interest. I was engaged the whole time.<br><br>HOWEVER . . .<br><br>I just didn’t find the twists shocking neither was I disturbed by the heinousness of it all. I mean, this book is absolutely sickening, but the horror didn’t jump off the pages and register to me (if that makes sense).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591721365ra/29619929.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was deeply moved by the family dynamics. My favorite part in this book is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the father’s POV/letters to the girls <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I wish I’d gotten more of the three sisters so that I could see more clearly the shift in their bond before/after the tragedy and their split.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You couldn’t turn on the TV without hearing about the missing teenage girl. Sixteen years old. White. Middle class. Very pretty. No one ever seemed quite as outraged when an ugly woman went missing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I’m a little concerned that there’s not a single decent male character in this book. Well, there’s one, but the man is dead. I’m also uncomfortable with the way beauty is viewed and how <i>Pretty Girls</i> is heavily centered around violence against women.<br><br>My biggest complaint is this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Why did it have to be her?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>WHY DID IT HAVE TO HAPPEN AT ALL? The book doesn’t provide any explanation why the crime is committed, why the perpetrator has a proclivity for such sadistic behavior and how it came to be. I was curious, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially because Paul is indoctrinated and groomed by his father to continue “the family business” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><b>
  <i>(Read as an Audiobook)</i>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5970906074571242977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770356509?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14283732532595271966">Wow! I have never read anything by Karin Slaughter before and I was a little bit apprehensive to start with this particular book because of some of the things I was hearing about the subject matter of this one. I thought it was absolutely one of the best dark, psychological thrillers that I have read! I am looking forward to reading m</span>
  <span id="freeText14283732532595271966" style="display:none">Wow! I have never read anything by Karin Slaughter before and I was a little bit apprehensive to start with this particular book because of some of the things I was hearing about the subject matter of this one. I thought it was absolutely one of the best dark, psychological thrillers that I have read! It was an absolutely intense read with shocking twists that had me totally engrossed in every single page I was reading! I could not put this down, it was so good! I am looking forward to reading more of her books in the future!<br /><br />PRETTY GIRLS is a story told in three different points of view; Claire, Lydia and their fathers journal/letter to Julia the sister who went missing over 20 years ago. Claire and Lydia are estranged but brought back together after a tragedy happens in Claire's life. I absolutely loved the interaction between these two characters as they unravel the truth and secrets from their past. <br /><br />This is by far one of the sickest psychopaths I've ever read about and the author does go into some graphic detail that might be disturbing for some. It didn't really bother me though as I tend to not put myself totally into those parts while reading. I am not a skimmer, I have to read every single word but I am able to detach myself while reading disturbing scenes. <br /><br />The author did an excellent job with the plot and character development which had me totally invested in what I was reading as the suspense and tension developed.<br /> <br />It was an intense, quick and disturbing fast-paced thriller with a very satisfying ending. Would recommend!<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a></span>

  <span id="freeText9512527388599456960" style="display:none"> So incredibly good!<br /><br />The shattering of a family as told from the perspective of the remaining members. <br /> <br />Julia goes missing one night at age 19, following an evening out with her college friends to a local bar. Julia's 2 sisters Claire and Lydia, grow up in the shadow of her disappearance and take different paths in their lives. <br /><br />24 years later her family remains in shambles. A recent, tragic event brings Julia and Lydia back together. Can they finally discover what happened to their sister? <br /><br />Shocking, disturbing, riveting. Can one feel all three at once? Get ready…this book takes you through all three emotions and more. Not for the faint of heart. If you like your thrillers a little dark and edgy then you will absolutely love this one!<br /><br />I was gripped by the story immediately, though I had no clue what direction I was being taken. Felt like a slow ride up a roller-coaster, where you know the story is building and once you reach the top it's all going to break free and explode at breakneck speed. And that's exactly what happens. What a great ride!<br /></span>

Pretty Girls is a story written by the talented Karin Slaughter, and the recurring feelings she conveys to us are full of pathos.   <span id="freeText5790583233208463432" style="display:none">You know you're getting long in the tooth when the book you're reading has a distant past set in 1990. That was the year I joined high school. The past has many treasured memories that I hold dear. But in many ways life was harder than now in societal terms.<br /><br />Which leads us to this book. Pretty Girls is a story written by the talented Karin Slaughter, and the recurring feelings she conveys to us are full of pathos. But she also does a professional job of thinking of convoluted and complex ways to make her story seem plausible. Check. And enjoyable. Check.<br /><br />There are revisits to the past. And there are multiple POVs in the book. I realize how difficult it is for a normal human being to keep writing books like this. But among a very small percent of wannabe writers, only a small pool of talent is able to maintain the kind of pacing that this book has.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217354509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14188254626247015279">I've not read anything before by Karin Slaughter. Believe me, this was probably not the one to start with. The subject matter is heavy, heavy, dark, dark.<br/><br/>Ms. Slaughter can give you precise, intricate details of a crime like no other. She makes you feel like you are watching your foot placement as you tread through the crime scene with bated breath. Your brain is filled with such terrible imaginings.<br/><br/>This story focuses on a missing sister from the past and a missing girl of the present. Karin Slau</span>
  <span id="freeText14188254626247015279" style="display:none">I've not read anything before by Karin Slaughter. Believe me, this was probably not the one to start with. The subject matter is heavy, heavy, dark, dark.<br /><br />Ms. Slaughter can give you precise, intricate details of a crime like no other. She makes you feel like you are watching your foot placement as you tread through the crime scene with bated breath. Your brain is filled with such terrible imaginings.<br /><br />This story focuses on a missing sister from the past and a missing girl of the present. Karin Slaughter writes with such emotion that peels away the deep and the hidden secrets that a family has carried for years and years. It deals with the agony of a father through his journals and we, as readers, are privy to such unspeakable loss that ripples across the pages.<br /><br />This is not just the telling of a horrendous crime. It is the fracturing within a family that chistles away at all that we hold precious and untouchable. This book leaves you totally unsettled within. Be prepared for that......<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14188254626247015279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1321076322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1321076322" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1321076322?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781473507876" href="/book/show/25109445-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carol by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2337007-brenda">Brenda</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=published-2015">published-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=chunkster">chunkster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=library-overdrive">library-overdrive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321076322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16507605452578683465"><i>"When you first disappeared, your mother warned me that finding out exactly what happened to you would be worse than never knowing."</i> Oh. How. True.<p><b>PRETTY GIRLS</b> is a story about the unexplained disappearance of one missing sister <i>(of three)</i> named Julia, and the devastating after-affects of her loss. It is also a story about a sick and sadistic psychopath who works his evil in despicable ways that are graphically described within these pages which should serve as a warning to those opposed to read</p></span>
  <span id="freeText16507605452578683465" style="display:none"><i>"When you first disappeared, your mother warned me that finding out exactly what happened to you would be worse than never knowing."</i> Oh. How. True.<p><b>PRETTY GIRLS</b> is a story about the unexplained disappearance of one missing sister <i>(of three)</i> named Julia, and the devastating after-affects of her loss. It is also a story about a sick and sadistic psychopath who works his evil in despicable ways that are graphically described within these pages which should serve as a warning to those opposed to reading such violence.</p><p>The story pulled me in right from the start, but was a bit confusing with regard to character connection for a bit until <i>"something"</i> happens in the alley that drew me back in, sorted out the players and kept my interest till the gratifying end.</p><p>Haven't read a Karin Slaughter novel in a <b>very</b> long time, but this stalker murder-mystery is a hell of a thriller with one hell of a shocker.....or two.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16507605452578683465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1864761634" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864761634" />
    <a title="Rebbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6582211-rebbie"><img alt="Rebbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430858965p2/6582211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864761634?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebbie" href="/user/show/6582211-rebbie">Rebbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6582211-rebbie?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864761634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9792344828222878339">This book might need a trigger warning for those with genuine PTSD because of its brutal violence. Normally I'd steer clear of suggesting that someone might have a hard time with a book, but this one is particularly gruesome and gory. <br/><br/>A lot of people like that sort of thing, but I personally felt overwhelmed beginning around the 30% mark, and it didn't really let up until the end. I didn't have a problem with the violence until that point, but then it just got to be too much, especially because </span>
  <span id="freeText9792344828222878339" style="display:none">This book might need a trigger warning for those with genuine PTSD because of its brutal violence. Normally I'd steer clear of suggesting that someone might have a hard time with a book, but this one is particularly gruesome and gory. <br /><br />A lot of people like that sort of thing, but I personally felt overwhelmed beginning around the 30% mark, and it didn't really let up until the end. I didn't have a problem with the violence until that point, but then it just got to be too much, especially because the nature of the brutality toward the rape and murder victims is extremely unsettling.<br /><br />I was hoping more for psychological torment, rather than relying on sheer shock value to carry the story. Of course, that's just my opinion, which is only worth what you paid for it. ;)<br /><br />I particularly loved the chapters where Julia's dad wrote her letters. Man, that ripped my heart out. It physically hurt to read the loving, fatherly tone, with his undying love for his missing daughter. The world could've ended, and he wouldn't have sacrificed his love for his daughter. Only death could bring sweet relief from the pain of missing your child. <br /><br />His chapters completely redeemed the book imo, and made it worthwhile to finish the book until the end. It shows that Karin Slaughter has some good writing chops, so I'll definitely check out her other work and give it a go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9792344828222878339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1308684534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1308684534" />
    <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady"><img alt="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601761303p2/22943325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1308684534?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxine (Booklover Catlady)" href="/user/show/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady">Maxine (Booklover Catlady)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24959571-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=dysfunctional-people">dysfunctional-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=psychological-thrillers-read">psychological-thrillers-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=favourite-authors-read">favourite-authors-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22943325-maxine-booklover-catlady?shelf=crime-books-read">crime-books-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1308684534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8002028601606138099">I've been late to the table as a Karin Slaughter fan, hard to believe as a crime fiction lover. I adored her book Cop Town and was excited to read this new stand alone thriller.<br/><br/><i>With a missing girl in the news, Claire Scott can’t help but be reminded of her sister, who disappeared twenty years ago in a mystery that was never solved.<br/><br/>But when Claire begins to learn the truth about her sister, nothing will ever be the same.</i><br/><br/>I found this book to have an interesting plot if somewhat up and down in pace</span>
  <span id="freeText8002028601606138099" style="display:none">I've been late to the table as a Karin Slaughter fan, hard to believe as a crime fiction lover. I adored her book Cop Town and was excited to read this new stand alone thriller.<br /><br /><i>With a missing girl in the news, Claire Scott can’t help but be reminded of her sister, who disappeared twenty years ago in a mystery that was never solved.<br /><br />But when Claire begins to learn the truth about her sister, nothing will ever be the same.</i><br /><br />I found this book to have an interesting plot if somewhat up and down in pace. Karin is without question an outstanding writer and all of her books have depth and detail that keeps you well aware of what's going on.<br /><br />I enjoyed more aspects of the plot than others but I'm not sharing any with you, so there. The characters are all very well done, enough damaged characters to keep me happy.<br /><br />The concept of finding out your husband is not who you thought he was has been tackled a lot in many genres of books but Karin tackles it from a very chilling and disturbing angle. I've been through this experience personally (not the version in the book thank God!)<br /><br />It's a book full of psychological twists, enough to keep to wondering, guessing and wanting more. I think this stand-alone book of Karin's may attract a new legion of fans discovering both her new books and the many successful books that have gone before.<br /><br />4 paw prints from Booklover Catlady for this one. Highly recommended reading!<br /><br />For more of my reviews find me at:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/BookloverCatlady">https://www.facebook.com/BookloverCat...</a><br /><br />Follow me on Twitter! I talk back!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.twitter.com/promotethatbook">https://www.twitter.com/promotethatbook</a> <br /><br /><i>I received a review copy if this book thanks to the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8002028601606138099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Katie B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b"><img alt="Katie B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469412116p2/49444196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463158992?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie B" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b">Katie B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062429056" href="/book/show/25465056-pretty-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=georgia">georgia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463158992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17589863202253037891">4.5 stars<br/><br/>It almost feels weird to say this book held my interest because it is such a dark and disturbing story. This is the third book I have read by the author and she's just a really good storyteller. I'm now going to make it more of a priority to seek out her other books because she has proven to me she is one of the best in the business.<br/><br/>Over twenty years ago, Julia vanished without a trace. To say her disappearance had an impact on her family is putting it mildly. Her two sisters, Claire an</span>
  <span id="freeText17589863202253037891" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />It almost feels weird to say this book held my interest because it is such a dark and disturbing story. This is the third book I have read by the author and she's just a really good storyteller. I'm now going to make it more of a priority to seek out her other books because she has proven to me she is one of the best in the business.<br /><br />Over twenty years ago, Julia vanished without a trace. To say her disappearance had an impact on her family is putting it mildly. Her two sisters, Claire and Lydia, haven't spoken in years. Lydia is a single mother and struggles to make ends meet while Claire is living a life of luxury. However, tragedy hits Claire's life once again when her husband is killed. When it appears there might be some link between Julia's disappearance and her husband's murder, Claire could use some help digging to find the truth. And Lydia might be the one to help her find some answers.<br /><br />One of the first thoughts I had when I finished this book was, wow that was good but probably not the most realistic story I have ever read. However given recent news stories, maybe this story isn't all that implausible. There are truly some sick and messed up individuals in this world and this book certainly highlights that fact. <br /><br />I feel like just about everyone has already read this book, but if you were like me and had this on your tbr list forever, I will say, make this one more of a priority to read! I do suggest though if subjects like sexual assault are difficult for you to read about, I recommend taking a pass on this book. I normally don't give warnings about content but this book does go into graphic detail and I think it's important to know that ahead of time so you can make the decision if this is the book for you.<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1338693493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1338693493" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1338693493?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=novella-short-story">novella-short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=edelweiss-review">edelweiss-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338693493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7003022519378486070"><br/>Karin Slaughter is a seasoned author of taut suspense and she certainly knows how to weave a wicked little tale. This one though was a real mind bender. <br/><br/>It's been over twenty years since Lydia and Claire's older sister, Julia, disappeared. Their lives took drastically different directions at that point, as Lydia falls into drug abuse and addiction, and Claire quietly disappears into the safe environment her genius husband, Paul, has created for her. Claire and Lydia have been estranged for all t</span>
  <span id="freeText7003022519378486070" style="display:none"><br />Karin Slaughter is a seasoned author of taut suspense and she certainly knows how to weave a wicked little tale. This one though was a real mind bender. <br /><br />It's been over twenty years since Lydia and Claire's older sister, Julia, disappeared. Their lives took drastically different directions at that point, as Lydia falls into drug abuse and addiction, and Claire quietly disappears into the safe environment her genius husband, Paul, has created for her. Claire and Lydia have been estranged for all these years, but when Paul is killed, the two sisters cautiously reconnect as they begin to uncover a mountain of lies, sins, crimes, and depravity, no one would ever have guessed at, and at the very heart of the matter, is the drive to discover what really happened to their sister all those years ago. <br /><br /><br />Once I started this book I was immediately sucked into it, and found it deeply absorbing. The book is longer than the usual three hundred and fifty page lengths I have grown used to, and while there is a vast amount of information to digest and weed through, there were times the story got bogged down a little and the momentum suffered as a result. A few times I questioned some of the information and found it pushed the boundaries of plausibility, but overall, the plot was tightly woven, clever, and very tense. The characters were well drawn and the baddies are particularly chilling. Although the story is basically centered around Claire, I didn't know what to think of her sometimes. Her character does grow in leaps and bounds and she discovers a strength within her she never knew she had. However, Lydia was inspirational, a character I liked instantly. She steals the show in many ways with her sharp mouth, her bravery and ability to forgive, which in the beginning was something she struggles with. <br /><br />This book is not for the faint of heart as the subject matter is very dark, the violence is graphic, and the imagery is quite disturbing. It is also a very emotional and heartbreaking story, as we see the toll the crimes have taken on the families.<br /> By the time I got the end, I felt like I had just finished a marathon or participated in the triathlon. This book gives your brain, your body and soul a thorough workout, but like Claire, Helen, and Lydia, I was left with a sense of peace, a feeling these strong women will survive their ordeal, and will pass that fortitude onto the next generation, making those who didn't live to see justice done, very proud indeed. <br /><br />4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="7003022519378486070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('djDahZNovoTgHvgkowQHv1q5BgYz8GpdsWdnvFIkgsfhIoEy4Yu202JT8E5Cc4bzBlf1eAWGOK85epYu0KY9tg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Up4+UbfUBxqHu64RUqjoSrqwB7NOzh/YEoqp33+mhlnFjGXmxTcPTQX2pnuz32kG5l70zXi4TSqal1hN/SQ5KA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter">About Karin Slaughter</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1565730670p3/12504.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6989593529230119550">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAS</span>
  <span id="freeText6989593529230119550" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAST WIDOW, features Sara Linton and Will Trent. Slaughter is the founder of the Save the Libraries project—a nonprofit organization established to support libraries and library programming. A native of Georgia, Karin Slaughter lives in Atlanta. Her standalone novels PIECES OF HER, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and COP TOWN are in development for film and television.<br /><br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter">Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter</a> <br /><br /><b>Website</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.karinslaughter.com/">http://www.karinslaughter.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/karinslaughterauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/karinslaugh...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6989593529230119550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Guys are hitting on them all of the time. They can't walk down the street or order a coffee or stand on a corner without some idiot making a comment about how attractive they are. And the women smile because it's easier than telling them to go fuck themselves. And less dangerous, because if a man rejects a woman, she goes home and cries for a few days. If a woman rejects a man, he can rape and kill her.&rdquo;</span>
